Beschikking 2005/513/EG van de Commissie<br>van 11 juli 2005 betreffende het geharmoniseerde<br>gebruik van het radiospectrum in de 5 GHz-<br>frequentieband voor de implementatie van draadloze<br>toegangssystemen met inbegrip van Radio Local Area<br>Networks (WAS/R-LAN’s) (PB L 187 van 19.7.2005,<br>blz. 22-24) Zie de geconsolideerde versie.<br>Richtlijn 91/287/EEG van de Raad van 3 juni 1991<br>betreffende de toewijzing van de frequentieband<br>voor de gecoördineerde invoering van digitale<br>Europese draadloze telecommunicatie (DECT) in de<br>Gemeenschap (PB L 144 van 8.6.1991, blz. 45-46)<br>GERELATEERDE DOCUMENTEN Richtlijn (EU) 2018/1972<br>van het Europees Parlement en de Raad van 11<br>december 2018 tot vaststelling van het Europees<br>wetboek voor elektronische communicatie<br>(herschikking) (PB L 321 van 17.12.2018, blz.<br>36-214) Zie de geconsolideerde versie. Beschikking<br>nr. 676/2002/EG van het Europees Parlement en de<br>Raad van 7 maart 2002 inzake een regelgevingskader<br>voor het radiospectrumbeleid in de Europese<br>Gemeenschap (Radiospectrumbeschikking) (PB L 108<br>van 24.4.2002, blz. 1-6) Laatste bijwerking<br>12.11.2020 | Dit is een samenvatting van Uitvoeringsbesluit<br>(EU) 2019/785 van de Commissie, van 14 mei 2019,<br>betreffende de harmonisatie van het radiospectrum<br>voor apparatuur die gebruikmaakt van<br>ultrabreedbandtechnologie (UWB) in de EU.  Het<br>besluit vervangt Beschikking 2007/131/EG en heeft<br>als doel een doelmatige en geharmoniseerde toegang<br>tot het radiospectrum voor UWB-apparatuur te<br>creëren, terwijl schadelijke interferentie met<br>andere diensten wordt voorkomen.  **Kernpunten:**<br>* **Harmonisatie:** Het besluit harmoniseert de<br>technische voorwaarden voor het gebruik van UWB-<br>technologie in de EU,  zowel voor generiek gebruik<br>als voor specifieke toepassingen. *<br>**Frequentiebanden:** Het besluit specificeert<br>maximale gemiddelde spectrale vermogensdichtheid<br>(e.i.r.p.) en maximaal piekvermogen (e.i.r.p.)<br>voor verschillende frequentiebanden. Deze waarden<br>variëren afhankelijk van de toepassing (generiek<br>gebruik, locatiebepaling, in voertuigen, in<br>vliegtuigen, materiaaldetectie). *<br>**Mitigatietechnieken:**  Het besluit schrijft<br>mitigatietechnieken voor om interferentie te<br>voorkomen, zoals "low duty cycle" (LDC), "detect<br>and avoid" (DAA), en "trigger before transmit".<br>Alternatieve technieken zijn toegestaan, mits ze<br>een gelijkwaardig niveau van spectrumbescherming<br>garanderen en voldoen aan de essentiële eisen van<br>Richtlijn 2014/53/EU. * **Toepassingen:** Het<br>besluit behandelt verschillende UWB-toepassingen,<br>waaronder generiek gebruik,<br>locatiebepalingssystemen (LT1), gebruik in<br>motorvoertuigen en spoorvoertuigen, gebruik aan<br>boord van vliegtuigen en materiaaldetectie (op<br>contact en niet-op-contact).  Voor elke toepassing<br>worden specifieke technische eisen gesteld. *<br>**Materiaaldetectie:**  Voor materiaaldetectie-<br>apparatuur worden specifieke, strengere<br>grenswaarden vastgesteld, afhankelijk van of het<br>apparaat contact maakt met het materiaal. Vaste<br>buiteninstallaties zijn voor materiaaldetectie in<br>bepaalde frequentiebanden uitgesloten. *<br>**Toezicht:** Lidstaten moeten toezicht houden op<br>het gebruik van de aangewezen frequentiebanden en<br>hun bevindingen aan de Commissie melden. *<br>**Intrekking:** Beschikking 2007/131/EG wordt<br>ingetrokken.  **In het kort:** Het besluit streeft<br>naar een evenwicht tussen het bevorderen van<br>innovatieve UWB-technologie en het beschermen van<br>bestaande radiocommunicatiediensten door het<br>definiëren van specifieke technische eisen en<br>mitigatietechnieken voor verschillende<br>toepassingen van UWB.  De bijlage bevat<br>uitgebreide tabellen met de technische eisen per<br>frequentieband en toepassing. |
| english | Prospectus to be published when securities are<br>offered to the public or admitted to trading on a<br>regulated market Prospectus to be published when<br>securities are offered to the public or admitted<br>to trading on a regulated market SUMMARY OF:<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979<br>supplementing Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on<br>regulatory technical standards on key financial<br>information in the summary of a prospectus, the<br>publication and classification of prospectuses,<br>advertisements for securities, supplements to a<br>prospectus, and the notification portal Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/980 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 on format, content, scrutiny and<br>approval of the prospectus to be published when<br>securities are offered to the public or admitted<br>to trading on a regulated market Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/528 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 on the minimum information content<br>of the document to be published for a prospectus<br>exemption in connection with a takeover by means<br>of an exchange offer, a merger or a division WHAT<br>IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION? Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 (the prospectus regulation), as<br>supplemented by Delegated Regulations (EU)<br>2019/979, 2019/980 and 2019/528, aims to help<br>companies, including small and medium-sized<br>enterprises (SMEs), access different forms of<br>finance in the European Union (EU). It does so by<br>simplifying and streamlining the rules and<br>procedures for drawing up, approving and<br>distributing the prospectus* they publish when<br>offering securities* to the public or admitting<br>securities to trading on a regulated market. The<br>legislation reduces costly and burdensome red tape<br>for companies and enables investors to make the<br>right investment decision by providing<br>comprehensible, easy to analyse and concise<br>information. KEY POINTS                The<br>regulation: removes the need for a prospectus for<br>any offer of securities to the public, including<br>crowdfunding (raising money from a large group of<br>people, often via the internet) projects, below €1<br>million (previously the limit was €100,000);<br>allows EU Member States to be exempt from the need<br>for a prospectus for offers of securities to the<br>public of up to €8 million, provided that they do<br>not require notification (a ‘passport’); sets out<br>rules to curb the tendency to overload<br>prospectuses with generic risk factors;<br>strengthens supervisory convergence by harmonising<br>scrutiny and approval of prospectuses (including<br>the applicable timelines) throughout the EU;<br>enables companies that frequently issue securities<br>to use the universal registration document to<br>secure fast-track approval from supervisors within<br>5 days; introduces a European online database,<br>operated free of charge by the European Securities<br>and Markets Authority (ESMA), containing all<br>prospectuses approved in the European Economic<br>Area. The regulation requires a prospectus to<br>enable an investor to make an informed decision.<br>It must include: assets, liabilities, profits,<br>losses, financial position and prospects for the<br>issuer and any guarantor; rights attached to the<br>securities; reasons for issuing the securities and<br>their impact on the issuer; a clear and accurate<br>seven-page summary (except for the admission to<br>trading of non-equity securities only targeting<br>qualified investors), which provides: an<br>introduction with warnings that the investor could<br>lose all or part of the invested capital,key<br>information on the securities, including the type<br>and class of securities and the rights attached to<br>the securities,information about the issuer,a<br>brief description of the nature and scope of a<br>guarantee. The regulation establishes a<br>standardised and simplified EU growth prospectus<br>for: SMEs, defined in Directive 2014/65/EU (the<br>MiFID II directive) (see summary) as companies<br>which meet at least two of the following three<br>criteria: an average number of employees during<br>the financial year of less than 250,a total<br>balance sheet not exceeding €43 million,an annual<br>net turnover not exceeding €50 million; issuers,<br>other than SMEs, whose securities are traded or to<br>be traded on an SME growth market (a market that<br>offers access to capital for SMEs), with an<br>average market capitalisation (market value of the<br>company’s shares) of below €500 million; offerors<br>of securities issued by issuers referred to in the<br>two previous points; non-listed companies (not<br>listed on any stock market) which offer securities<br>to the public of less than €20 million in any<br>given 12 months, provided that they have fewer<br>than 500 employees; issuers, other than SMEs, that<br>offer shares to the public and at the same time<br>seek admission of those shares to trading on an<br>SME growth market, provided that: such issuers<br>have no shares already admitted to trading on an<br>SME growth market,the combined value of the final<br>offer price (or, if not available, the maximum<br>price) and the total number of shares outstanding<br>immediately after the share offer to the public is<br>less than €200 million. The abovementioned<br>companies can benefit from this tailored<br>prospectus provided that they have no securities<br>admitted to trading on a regulated market. The<br>regulation provides for a simplified prospectus<br>for companies listed for at least 18 months on a<br>regulated market or an SME growth market and<br>wishing to issue additional shares or raise debt<br>(secondary issuance). The regulation harmonises<br>the minimum information content of the document to<br>be published for a prospectus exemption in<br>connection with a takeover by means of an exchange<br>offer, a merger or a division. Amending<br>regulations Regulation (EU) 2019/2115 seeks to<br>promote the use of SME growth markets by reducing<br>formalities and administrative burdens on SMEs in<br>terms of disclosure obligations and a simplified<br>prospectus. Regulation (EU) 2020/1503 introduces a<br>prospectus exemption for offers of securities to<br>the public made by crowdfunding service providers<br>that do not exceed the threshold of €5 million in<br>accordance with the conditions specified in that<br>regulation. Regulation (EU) 2021/337 introduces a<br>new ‘EU recovery prospectus’ to help companies<br>recover from the COVID-19 crisis. This shorter<br>prospectus, with a maximum length of 30 pages plus<br>a two-page summary, makes it easier for companies<br>to raise capital to meet their funding needs,<br>while ensuring adequate information is provided to<br>investors. The recovery prospectus will be<br>available for capital increases of up to 150% of<br>outstanding capital within a period of 12 months<br>and applies until the end of 2022. Delegated acts<br>The European Commission has adopted the following<br>acts. Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/980 laying<br>down details of the precise content and format of<br>the prospectus, as well as concerning the scrutiny<br>and approval of the prospectus. Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/979 laying down details of<br>the key financial information in the summary of<br>the prospectus, the publication and classification<br>of the prospectus, the advertisement for the<br>securities and the supplement to a prospectus.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2020/1273 amending and<br>correcting Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/980.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2020/1272 amending and<br>correcting Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2021/528 setting out the<br>minimum information content of the document to be<br>published for a prospectus exemption in connection<br>with a takeover by means of an exchange offer, a<br>merger or a division. Report The Commission is<br>required to report on the application of the<br>legislation before 21 July 2022. FROM WHEN DO THE<br>REGULATIONS APPLY? Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 and<br>Delegated Regulations (EU) 2019/979 and (EU)<br>2019/980 have applied since 21 July 2019.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2021/528 has applied<br>since 15 April 2021. BACKGROUND Directive<br>2003/71/EC was designed to make it easier for<br>companies to raise capital throughout the EU on<br>the basis of approval from just one national<br>supervisor. This gave a ‘passport’ for<br>prospectuses containing cross-border offers.<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129, which repeals and<br>replaces Directive 2003/71/EEC, addresses the<br>areas of legal uncertainty and unjustified<br>administrative burdens which had emerged over<br>time. It is considered a major milestone towards a<br>European capital markets union. For further<br>information, see: Securities prospectus (European<br>Commission) Prospectus (European Securities and<br>Markets Authority). KEY TERMS<br>Prospectus. A legal document describing a<br>company’s main line of business, finances and<br>shareholding structure. Potential investors use it<br>to decide whether to buy the securities a company<br>offers. Securities. Shares, bonds and derivatives.<br>MAIN DOCUMENTS              Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of the<br>Council of 14 June 2017 on the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market, and repealing Directive 2003/71/EC (OJ L<br>168, 30.6.2017, pp. 12–82). Successive amendments<br>to Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 have been<br>incorporated in the original text. This<br>consolidated version is of documentary value only.<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979 of<br>14 March 2019 supplementing Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of the<br>Council with regard to regulatory technical<br>standards on key financial information in the<br>summary of a prospectus, the publication and<br>classification of prospectuses, advertisements for<br>securities, supplements to a prospectus, and the<br>notification portal, and repealing Commission<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) No 382/2014 and<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2016/301 (OJ<br>L 166, 21.6.2019, pp. 1–25). See consolidated<br>version. Commission Delegated Regulation (EU)<br>2019/980 of 14 March 2019 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council as regards the format, content,<br>scrutiny and approval of the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market, and repealing Commission Regulation (EC)<br>No 809/2004 (OJ L 166, 21.6.2019, pp. 26–176). See<br>consolidated version. Commission Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/528 of 16 December 2020<br>supplementing Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 of the<br>European Parliament and of the Council as regards<br>the minimum information content of the document to<br>be published for a prospectus exemption in<br>connection with a takeover by means of an exchange<br>offer, a merger or a division (OJ L 106,<br>26.3.2021, pp. 32–46). RELATED DOCUMENTS<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/337 of the European<br>Parliament and of the Council of 16 February 2021<br>amending Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 as regards the<br>EU Recovery prospectus and targeted adjustments<br>for financial intermediaries and Directive<br>2004/109/EC as regards the use of the single<br>electronic reporting format for annual financial<br>reports, to support the recovery from the COVID-19<br>crisis (OJ L 68, 26.2.2021, pp. 1–13). Regulation<br>(EU) 2020/1503 of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council of 7 October 2020 on European<br>crowdfunding service providers for business, and<br>amending Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 and Directive<br>(EU) 2019/1937 (OJ L 347, 20.10.2020, pp. 1–49).<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/2115 of the European<br>Parliament and of the Council of 27 November 2019<br>amending Directive 2014/65/EU and Regulations (EU)<br>No 596/2014 and (EU) 2017/1129 as regards the<br>promotion of the use of SME growth markets (OJ L<br>320, 11.12.2019, pp. 1–10). last update 22.11.2021 | This document is Commission Delegated Regulation<br>(EU) 2019/980 of 14 March 2019, supplementing<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on prospectuses for<br>securities offered to the public or admitted to<br>trading on a regulated market.  It specifies the<br>format, content, scrutiny, and approval of<br>prospectuses, repealing Commission Regulation (EC)<br>No 809/2004.  **Key aspects of the regulation<br>include:**  * **Prospectus Content:**  The<br>regulation details minimum information<br>requirements for various types of registration<br>documents and securities notes, differentiating<br>based on issuer type (e.g., SMEs, closed-end<br>collective investment undertakings, third-country<br>issuers), security type (equity vs. non-equity,<br>retail vs. wholesale), and issuance type (primary<br>vs. secondary).  It addresses specific information<br>needs for complex financial histories, significant<br>financial commitments, securities convertible into<br>shares, asset-backed securities, and guarantees.<br>Issuers are allowed flexibility in the order of<br>information, except for certain standardized<br>formats like the EU Growth prospectus.  *<br>**Prospectus Format:** The regulation specifies<br>the format of prospectuses (single document or<br>separate documents), base prospectuses, and final<br>terms, defining the order of information and<br>allowing for blanks in the base prospectus to be<br>filled in the final terms.  It clarifies the use<br>of "summary" and requires a clear table of<br>contents.  * **EU Growth Prospectus:** This<br>simplified prospectus for SMEs has specific,<br>standardized format and content requirements for<br>registration documents and securities notes for<br>both equity and non-equity securities.  A maximum<br>length is set for the specific summary.  *<br>**Scrutiny and Approval:** Harmonized criteria for<br>scrutinizing prospectuses are established,<br>focusing on completeness, comprehensibility, and<br>consistency.  Competent authorities can apply<br>additional criteria where necessary for investor<br>protection.  A proportionate approach is allowed<br>for similar prospectuses or those incorporating<br>information already scrutinized.  Submission must<br>be in searchable electronic format.  Subsequent<br>drafts must include marked-up and clean versions.<br>* **Definitions:**  The regulation provides<br>definitions for key terms such as "asset-backed<br>securities," "equivalent third-country market,"<br>"profit estimate," "profit forecast," and<br>"significant gross change."  * **Repeal:**<br>Commission Regulation (EC) No 809/2004 is<br>repealed.  * **Enforcement:** The regulation is<br>binding in its entirety and directly applicable in<br>all Member States from July 21, 2019.  Numerous<br>annexes provide detailed specifications for each<br>information item required in the different<br>prospectus types. |

equipment<br>Decision 2010/368/EU amending Decision 2006/771/EC<br>on harmonisation of the radio spectrum for use by<br>short-range devices Decision 2009/381/EC amending<br>Decision 2006/771/EC on harmonisation of the radio<br>spectrum for use by short-range devices Decision<br>2007/90/EC amending Decision 2005/513/EC on the<br>harmonised use of radio spectrum in the 5 GHz<br>frequency band for the implementation of Wireless<br>Access Systems including Radio Local Area Networks<br>(WAS/RLANs) Decision 2008/411/EC on the<br>harmonisation of the 3 400-3 800 MHz frequency<br>band for terrestrial systems capable of providing<br>electronic communications services Decision<br>2005/513/EC on the harmonised use of radio<br>spectrum in the 5 GHz frequency band for the<br>implementation of wireless access systems<br>including radio local area networks (WAS/RLANs)<br>Directive 91/287/EEC on the frequency band to be<br>designated for the coordinated introduction of<br>digital European cordless telecommunications<br>(DECT) into the Community WHAT ARE THE AIMS OF THE<br>DIRECTIVE AND DECISIONS? The implementing<br>decisions mostly concern harmonisation, while<br>others deal with specific frequency bands for<br>specific purposes, in addition to limits on signal<br>strength and harmful interference where<br>applicable. EU countries are responsible for radio<br>spectrum management, and the amendments reflect<br>how European and international harmonisation and<br>technical agreements have evolved. The ‘DECT’<br>directive designates the 1 880-1 900 MHz frequency<br>band for digital cordless communications by 1<br>January 1992 and obliges EU countries to bring<br>into force the necessary national laws,<br>regulations and administrative rules. KEY POINTS<br>The decisions The implementing decisions cover<br>radio equipment devices that are operated through<br>general authorisation or on an unlicensed or<br>shared basis by end-users. This includes radio<br>local access network devices (wi-fi) devices which<br>have shown massive growth in demand for radio<br>spectrum, as acknowledged in the 2018 European<br>Electronic Communications Code. Many of these acts<br>are harmonisation decisions. Others deal with<br>frequency bands for different purposes, such as a<br>huge variety of short range devices, Internet of<br>Things (IoT) equipment, ultra-wide band equipment,<br>alarms, door openers, medical implants,<br>intelligent transport systems, radio frequency<br>identification devices (RFID), radio<br>determination, ground probing, and new types of<br>machine-to-machine devices, as well as equipment<br>for programme making and special events (PMSE)<br>such as wireless video links or microphones and<br>digital cordless telephones. A further general<br>authorisation band relates to vehicle safety, in<br>particular to the operation of Intelligent<br>Transport Systems (ITS). The various implementing<br>decisions cover the following radio spectrum, in<br>addition to limits on signal strength and harmful<br>interference where applicable: the 5 GHz frequency<br>band (5 150-5 350 MHz and 5 470-5 725 MHz) for<br>wireless access systems, including radio local<br>area networks (WAS/RLANs — wi-fi broadband); the 3<br>400-3 800 MHz frequency band for terrestrial<br>systems for ‘fixed, nomadic and mobile electronic<br>communications networks’; the 5 875-5 935 MHz<br>frequency band for safety-related applications of<br>Intelligent Transport Systems; the radio spectrum<br>for use by short-range devices; the 24 GHz range<br>radio spectrum band for the time-limited use by<br>automotive short-range radar equipment; radio<br>spectrum use by wireless audio programme-making<br>and special events equipment; the 2 010-2 025 MHz<br>frequency band for portable or mobile wireless<br>video links and cordless cameras used for<br>programme making and special events; the 900 MHz<br>and 1 800 MHz frequency bands for terrestrial<br>systems capable of providing electronic<br>communications services in relation to the<br>Internet of Things; radio spectrum for use by<br>short-range devices within the 874-876 and 915-921<br>MHz frequency bands; radio spectrum for equipment<br>using ultra-wideband technology, such as vehicle<br>and aircraft location tracking. Directive<br>91/287/EEC The directive obliges EU countries to<br>designate the 1 880-1 900 MHz frequency band for<br>digital cordless communications by 1 January 1992.<br>FROM WHEN DO THE DIRECTIVE AND DECISIONS APPLY?<br>Legislation Application date Implementing Decision<br>(EU) 2020/1426 8 October 2020 Implementing<br>Decision (EU) 2019/785 16 May 2019 Implementing<br>Decision (EU) 2018/1538 12 October 2018<br>Implementing Decision (EU) 2018/637 23 April 2018<br>Implementing Decision (EU) 2017/2077 13 November<br>2017 Implementing Decision (EU) 2017/1483 10<br>August 2017 Implementing Decision (EU) 2016/339 9<br>March 2016 Implementing Decision 2014/641/EU 2<br>September 2014 Implementing Decision 2013/752/EU<br>12 December 2013 Implementing Decision 2011/829/EU<br>9 December 2011 Implementing Decision 2011/485/EU<br>1 August 2011 Decision 2010/368/EU 1 July 2010<br>Decision 2009/381/EC 14 May 2009 Decision<br>2007/90/EC 12 February 2007 Decision 2008/411/EC<br>21 May 2008 Decision 2005/513/EC 11 July 2005<br>Directive 91/287/EEC 5 June 1991 BACKGROUND<br>For more information, see: What is Radio Spectrum<br>Policy? Council Directive 91/287/EEC of 3 June<br>1991 on the frequency band to be designated for<br>the coordinated introduction of digital European<br>cordless telecommunications (DECT) into the<br>Community (OJ L 144, 8.6.1991, pp. 45-46) RELATED<br>DOCUMENTS              Directive (EU) 2018/1972 of<br>the European Parliament and of the Council of 11<br>December 2018 establishing the European Electronic<br>Communications Code (Recast) (OJ L 321,<br>17.12.2018, pp. 36-214) See consolidated version.<br>Decision No 676/2002/EC of the European Parliament<br>and of the Council of 7 March 2002on a regulatory<br>framework for radio spectrum policy in the<br>European Community (Radio Spectrum Decision) (OJ L<br>108, 24.4.2002, pp. 1-6) last update 12.11.2020 | This European Commission Implementing Decision<br>(EU) 2019/785, effective May 14, 2019, harmonizes<br>radio spectrum use for ultra-wideband (UWB)<br>technology within the European Union.  It repeals<br>Decision 2007/131/EC.  The decision aims to create<br>a single market for UWB systems while mitigating<br>potential interference with existing services,<br>including radio astronomy.  The decision<br>establishes technical conditions for UWB<br>equipment, including power limits (maximum mean<br>power spectral density and maximum peak power)<br>across various frequency bands.  These limits vary<br>depending on the type of UWB application:  *<br>**Generic UWB Usage:**  Applies indoors and<br>outdoors (excluding fixed installations).  Power<br>limits are specified for different frequency<br>ranges (e.g., -90 dBm/MHz at f ≤ 1.6 GHz). *<br>**Location Tracking Systems Type 1 (LT1):**<br>Unlicensed operation; similar power limits to<br>generic usage. * **UWB Devices in Motor and<br>Railway Vehicles:**  Specific power limits are<br>set, with options for mitigation techniques like<br>Low Duty Cycle (LDC), Detect and Avoid (DAA), and<br>Transmit Power Control (TPC) in certain bands.  A<br>"trigger-before-transmit" mitigation is introduced<br>for vehicular access systems in the 3.8-4.2 GHz<br>and 6-8.5 GHz bands. * **UWB Onboard Aircraft:**<br>Specific power limits and mitigation requirements,<br>including notched filtering in certain frequency<br>ranges to protect satellite services, are defined.<br>* **Material Sensing Devices:** Divided into<br>contact and non-contact types, each with specific<br>power limits and requirements for mitigation<br>techniques, including Listen Before Talk (LBT).<br>Fixed outdoor installations are generally<br>prohibited in specific frequency ranges.  Member<br>States are required to allocate the specified<br>radio spectrum within six months and monitor its<br>use, reporting findings to the Commission.  The<br>decision also allows for alternative mitigation<br>techniques if they provide equivalent spectrum<br>protection and comply with Directive 2014/53/EU.<br>The Annex provides detailed technical requirements<br>(frequency ranges, power limits) for each UWB<br>application type. |
